# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Prometheus WAL Write-Ahead Log Segment Management

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in prometheus/prometheus that implement the TSDB write-ahead log (WAL): the WAL segment creation and rotation, the WAL record encoding (series, samples, tombstones), the WAL repair on corrupt segments, and the checkpoint creation to truncate old WAL data.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

Perfect! I've successfully completed the analysis of the Prometheus TSDB write-ahead log (WAL) implementation. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've identified **8 core Go source files** that implement the Prometheus TSDB WAL system:

### Core Files:
1. **tsdb/wlog/wlog.go** - Main WAL segment management (creation, rotation, repair)
2. **tsdb/wlog/reader.go** - WAL record reader with CRC validation
3. **tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go** - Live WAL reader for in-progress segments
4. **tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go** - Checkpoint creation for WAL truncation
5. **tsdb/wlog/watcher.go** - WAL monitoring and change dispatch
6. **tsdb/record/record.go** - Record encoding/decoding (series, samples, tombstones, histograms)
7. **tsdb/repair.go** - General TSDB repair utilities
8. **tsdb/head_wal.go** - WAL integration with the head block

### Key Symbols (60+ identified):
- **Segment Management**: `CreateSegment`, `OpenWriteSegment`, `NextSegment`, `NextSegmentSync`
- **Repair**: `Repair`, `CorruptionErr`
- **Record Types**: `RefSeries`, `RefSample`, `RefHistogramSample`, `RefFloatHistogramSample`, `RefExemplar`
- **Encoding**: `Encoder`, `Decoder`, `EncodeHistogram`, `DecodeHistogram`, `EncodeLabels`
- **Checkpoint**: `Checkpoint`, `LastCheckpoint`, `DeleteCheckpoints`, `CheckpointStats`
- **Readers**: `Reader`, `LiveReader`, `NewReader`, `NewLiveReader`
- **Watching**: `Watcher`, `WriteTo`

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file lists, symbol definitions, a functional chain showing WAL operation flow, and detailed narrative explaining each component's role in the crash-safe, page-based WAL system.

*WL) run() {\\n381: Loop:\\n382: \\tfor {\\n383: \\t\\tselect {\\n384: \\t\\tcase f := <-w.actorc:\\n385: \\t\\t\\tf()\\n386: \\t\\tcase donec := <-w.stopc:\\n387: \\t\\t\\tclose(w.actorc)\\n388: \\t}\\n396: }\\n397: \\n398: // Repair attempts to repair the WAL based on the error.\\n399: // It discards all data after the corruption.\\n400: func (w *WL) Repair(origErr error) error {\\n401: \\t// We could probably have a mode that only discards torn records right around\\n402: \\t// the corruption to preserve as data much as possible.\\n403: \\t// But that's not generally applicable if the records have any kind of causality.\\n404: \\t// Maybe as an extra mode in the future if mid-WAL corruptions become\\n405: \\t// a frequent concern.\\n406: \\tvar cerr *CorruptionErr\\n407: \\tif !errors.As(origErr, &cerr) {\\n408: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"cannot handle error: %w\\\", origErr)\\n409: \\t}\\n410: \\tif cerr.Segment < 0 {\\n411: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"corruption error does not specify position\\\")\\n412: \\t}\\n413: \\tw.logger.Warn(\\\"Starting corruption repair\\\",\\n414: \\t\\t\\\"segment\\\", cerr.Segment, \\\"offset\\\", cerr.Offset)\\n415: \\n416: \\t// All segments behind the corruption can no longer be used.\\n417: \\tsegs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\\n418: \\tif err != nil {\\n419: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"list segments: %w\\\", err)\\n420: \\t}\\n421: \\tw.logger.Warn(\\\"Deleting all segments newer than corrupted segment\\\", \\\"segment\\\", cerr.Segment)\\n422: \\n423: \\tfor _, s := range segs {\\n424: \\t\\tif w.segment.i == s.index {\\n425: \\t\\t\\t// The active segment needs to be removed,\\n426: \\t\\t\\t// close it first (Windows!). Can be closed safely\\n427: \\t\\t\\t// as we set the current segment to repaired file\\n428: \\t\\t\\t// below.\\n429: \\t\\t\\tif err := w.segment.Close(); err != nil {\\n430: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"close active segment: %w\\\", err)\\n431: \\t\\t\\t}\\n432: \\t\\t}\\n433: \\t\\tif s.index <= cerr.Segment {\\n434: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n435: \\t\\t}\\n436: \\t\\tif err := os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), s.name)); If no more records will fit into\\n581: // the page, the remaining bytes will be set to zero and a new page will be started.\\n582: // If forceClear is true, this is enforced regardless of how many bytes are left in the page.\\n583: func (w *WL) flushPage(forceClear bool) error {\\n584: \\tw.metrics.pageFlushes.Inc()\\n585: \\n586: \\tp := w.page\\n587: \\tshouldClear := forceClear || p.full()\\n588: \\n589: \\t// No more data will fit into the page or an implicit clear.\\n590: \\t// Enqueue and clear it.\\n591: \\tif shouldClear {\\n592: \\t\\tp.alloc = pageSize // Write till end of page.\\n593: \\t}\\n594: \\n595: \\tn, err := w.segment.Write(p.buf[p.flushed:p.alloc])\\n596: \\tif err != nil {\\n597: \\t\\tp.flushed += n\\n598: \\t\\treturn err\\n599: \\t}\\n600: \\tp.flushed += n\\n601: \\n602: \\t// We flushed an entire page, prepare a new one.\\n603: \\tif shouldClear {\\n604: \\t\\tp.reset()\\n605: \\t\\tw.donePages++\\n606: \\t\\tw.metrics.pageCompletions.Inc()\\n607: \\t}\\n608: \\treturn nil\\n609: }\\n610: \\n611: // First Byte of header format:\\n612: //\\n613: //\\t[3 bits unallocated] [1 bit zstd compression flag] [1 bit snappy compression flag] [3 bit record type ]\\n614: const (\\n615: \\tsnappyMask  = 1 << 3\\n616: \\tzstdMask    = 1 << 4\\n617: \\trecTypeMask = snappyMask - 1\\n618: )\\n619: \\n620: type recType uint8\\n621: \\n622: const (\\n623: \\trecPageTerm recType = 0 // Rest of page is empty.\\n624: \\trecFull     recType = 1 // Full record.\\n625: \\trecFirst    recType = 2 // First fragment of a record.\\n626: \\trecMiddle   recType = 3 // Middle fragments of a record.\\n627: \\trecLast     recType = 4 // Final fragment of a record.\\n628: )\\n629: \\n630: func recTypeFromHeader(header byte) recType {\\n631: \\treturn recType(header & recTypeMask)\\n632: }\\n633: \\n634: func (t recType) String() string {\\n635: \\tswitch t {\\n636: \\tcase recPageTerm:\\n637: \\t\\treturn \\\"zero\\\"\\n638: \\tcase recFull:\\n639: \\t\\treturn \\\"full\\\"\\n640: \\tcase recFirst:\\n641: \\t\\treturn \\\"first\\\"\\n642: \\tcase recMiddle:\\n643: \\t\\treturn \\\"middle\\\"\\n644: \\tcase recLast:\\n645: \\t\\treturn \\\"last\\\"\\n646: \\tdefault:\\n647: \\t\\treturn \\\"<invalid>\\\"\\n648: \\t}\\n649: }\\n650: \\n651: func (w *WL) pagesPerSegment() int {\\n652: \\treturn w.segmentSize / pageSize\\n653: }\\n654: \\n655: // Log writes the records into the log.\\n656: // Multiple records can be passed at once to reduce writes and increase throughput.\\n657: func (w *WL) Log(recs ...[]byte) error {\\n658: \\tw.mtx.Lock()\\n659: \\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\\n660: \\t// Callers could just implement their own list record format but adding\\n661: \\t// a bit of extra logic here frees them from that overhead.\\n662: \\tfor i, r := range recs {\\n663: \\t\\tif err := w.log(r, i == len(recs)-1); err != nil {\\n664: \\t\\t\\tw.metrics.writesFailed.Inc()\\n665: \\t\\t\\treturn err\\n666: \\t\\t}\\n667: \\t}\\n668: \\treturn nil\\n669: }\\n670: \\n671: // log writes rec to the log and forces a flush of the current page if:\\n672: // - len(enc)\\n692: \\n693: \\t\\t// Even if the compression was applied, skip it, if there's no benefit\\n694: \\t\\t// in the WAL record size (we have a choice). For small records e.g. snappy\\n695: \\t\\t// compression can yield larger records than the uncompressed.\\n696: \\t\\tif savedBytes <= 0 {\\n697: \\t\\t\\tenc = rec\\n698: \\t\\t\\tfinalCompression = compression.None\\n699: \\t\\t\\tsavedBytes = 0\\n700: \\t\\t}\\n701: \\t\\tw.metrics.recordBytesSaved.WithLabelValues(w.compress).Add(float64(savedBytes))\\n702: \\t}\\n703: \\n704: \\t// If the record is too big to fit within the active page in the current\\n705: \\t// segment, terminate the active segment and advance to the next one.\\n706: \\t// This ensures that records do not cross segment boundaries.\\n707: \\tleft := w.page.remaining() - recordHeaderSize                                   // Free space in the active page.\\n708: \\tleft += (pageSize - recordHeaderSize) * (w.pagesPerSegment() - w.donePages - 1) // Free pages in the active segment.\\n709: \\n710: \\tif len(enc) > left {\\n711: \\t\\tif _, err := w.nextSegment(true); We have to be careful not to increment curr too\\n959: // early, as it is used by Reader.Err() to tell Repair which segment is corrupt.\\n960: // As such we pad the end of non-page align segments with zeros.\\n961: type segmentBufReader struct {\\n962: \\tbuf  *bufio.Reader\\n963: \\tsegs []*Segment\\n964: \\tcur  int // Index into segs.\\n965: \\toff  int // Offset of read data into current segment.\\n966: }\\n967: \\n968: func NewSegmentBufReader(segs ...*Segment) io.ReadCloser {\\n969: \\tif len(segs) == 0 {\\n970: \\t\\treturn &segmentBufReader{}\\n971: \\t}\\n972: \\n973: \\treturn &segmentBufReader{\\n974: \\t\\tbuf:  bufio.NewReaderSize(segs[0], 16*pageSize),\\n975: \\t\\tsegs: segs,\\n976: \\t}\\n977: }\\n978: \\n979: func NewSegmentBufReaderWithOffset(offset int, segs ...*Segment) (io.ReadCloser, error) {\\n980: \\tif offset == 0 || len(segs) == 0 {\\n981: \\t\\treturn NewSegmentBufReader(segs...), nil\\n982: \\t}\\n983: \\n984: \\tsbr := &segmentBufReader{\\n985: \\t\\tbuf:  bufio.NewReaderSize(segs[0], 16*pageSize),\\n986: \\t\\tsegs: segs,\\n987: \\t}\\n988: \\tvar err error\\n989: \\tif offset > 0 {\\n990: \\t\\t_, err = sbr.buf.Discard(offset)\\n991: \\t}\\n992: \\treturn sbr, err\\n993: }\\n994: \\n995: func (r *segmentBufReader) Close() (err error) {\\n996: \\tfor _, s := range r.segs {\\n997: \\t\\tif e := s.Close(); e != nil {\\n998: \\t\\t\\terr = e\\n999: \\t\\t}\\n1000: \\t}\\n1001: \\treturn err\\n1002: }\\n1003: \\n1004: // Read implements io.Reader.\\n1005: func (r *segmentBufReader) Read(b []byte) (n int, err error) {\\n1006: \\tif len(r.segs) == 0 {\\n1007: \\t\\treturn 0, io.EOF\\n1008: \\t}\\n1009: \\n1010: \\tn, err = r.buf.Read(b)\\n1011: \\tr.off += n\\n1012: \\n1013: \\t// If we succeeded, or hit a non-EOF, we can stop.\\n1014: \\tif err == nil || !errors.Is(err, io.EOF) {\\n1015: \\t\\treturn n, err\\n1016: \\t}\\n1017: \\n1018: \\t// We hit EOF; n+i < len(b) && (r.off+i)%pageSize != 0; i++ {\\n1023: \\t\\t\\tb[n+i] = 0\\n1024: \\t\\t}\\n1025: \\n1026: \\t\\t// Return early, even if we didn't fill b.\\n1027: \\t\\tr.off += i\\n1028: \\t\\treturn n + i, nil\\n1029: \\t}\\n1030: \\n1031: \\t// There is no more deta left in the curr segment and there are no more\\n1032: \\t// segments left.  Return EOF.\\n1033: \\tif r.cur+1 >= len(r.segs) {\\n1034: \\t\\treturn n, io.EOF\\n1035: \\t}\\n1036: \\n1037: \\t// Move to next segment.\\n1038: \\tr.cur++\\n1039: \\tr.off = 0\\n1040: \\tr.buf.Reset(r.segs[r.cur])\\n1041: \\treturn n, nil\\n1042: }\\n1043: \\n1044: // Size computes the size of the write log.\\n1045: // We do this by adding the sizes of all the files under the WAL dir.\\n1046: func (w *WL) Size() (int64, error) {\\n1047: \\treturn fileutil.DirSize(w.Dir())\\n1048: }\\n1049: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/prometheus/prometheus@1751685dd4f6430757ba3078a96cffeffcb2bb47/-/blob/tsdb/wlog/wlog.go\"}",

SetWriteNotified(wn WriteNotified) {\n377: \tw.WriteNotified = wn\n378: }\n379: \n380: func (w *WL) run() {\n381: Loop:\n382: \tfor {\n383: \t\tselect {\n384: \t\tcase f := <-w.actorc:\n385: \t\t\tf()\n386: \t\tcase donec := <-w.stopc:\n387: \t\t\tclose(w.actorc)\n388: \t\t\tdefer close(donec)\n389: \t\t\tbreak Loop\n390: \t\t}\n391: \t}\n392: \t// Drain and process any remaining functions.\n393: \tfor f := range w.actorc {\n394: \t\tf()\n395: \t}\n396: }\n397: \n398: // Repair attempts to repair the WAL based on the error.\n399: // It discards all data after the corruption.\n400: func (w *WL) Repair(origErr error) error {\n401: \t// We could probably have a mode that only discards torn records right around\n402: \t// the corruption to preserve as data much as possible.\n403: \t// But that's not generally applicable if the records have any kind of causality.\n404: \t// Maybe as an extra mode in the future if mid-WAL corruptions become\n405: \t// a frequent concern.\n406: \tvar cerr *CorruptionErr\n407: \tif !errors.As(origErr, &cerr) {\n408: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"cannot handle error: %w\", origErr)\n409: \t}\n410: \tif cerr.Segment < 0 {\n411: \t\treturn errors.New(\"corruption error does not specify position\")\n412: \t}\n413: \tw.logger.Warn(\"Starting corruption repair\",\n414: \t\t\"segment\", cerr.Segment, \"offset\", cerr.Offset)\n415: \n416: \t// All segments behind the corruption can no longer be used.\n417: \tsegs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\n418: \tif err != nil {\n419: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"list segments: %w\", err)\n420: \t}\n421: \tw.logger.Warn(\"Deleting all segments newer than corrupted segment\", \"segment\", cerr.Segment)\n422: \n423: \tfor _, s := range segs {\n424: \t\tif w.segment.i == s.index {\n425: \t\t\t// The active segment needs to be removed,\n426: \t\t\t// close it first (Windows!). Can be closed safely\n427: \t\t\t// as we set the current segment to repaired file\n428: \t\t\t// below.\n429: \t\t\tif err := w.segment.Close(); err != nil {\n430: \t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"close active segment: %w\", err)\n431: \t\t\t}\n432: \t\t}\n433: \t\tif s.index <= cerr.Segment {\n434: \t\t\tcontinue\n435: \t\t}\n436: \t\tif err := os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), s.name)); err != nil {\n437: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"delete segment:%v: %w\", s.index, err)\n438: \t\t}\n439: \t}\n440: \t// Regardless of the corruption offset, no record reaches into the previous segment.\n441: \t// So we can safely repair the WAL by removing the segment and re-inserting all\n442: \t// its records up to the corruption.\n443: \tw.logger.Warn(\"Rewrite corrupted segment\", \"segment\", cerr.Segment)\n444: \n445: \tfn := SegmentName(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\n446: \ttmpfn := fn + \".repair\"\n447: \n448: \tif err := fileutil.Rename(fn, tmpfn); err != nil {\n449: \t\treturn err\n450: \t}\n451: \t// Create a clean segment and make it the active one.\n452: \ts, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\n453: \tif err != nil {\n454: \t\treturn err\n455: \t}\n456: \tif err := w.setSegment(s); \\t\\t\\t}\\n587: \\t\\t}\\n588: \\n589: \\t\\thistograms = append(histograms, rh)\\n590: \\t}\\n591: \\n592: \\tif dec.Err() != nil {\\n593: \\t\\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\\\"decode error after %d resetSeriesWithMMappedChunks(mSeries *memSeries, mmc, oooMmc []*mmappedChunk, walSeriesRef chunks.HeadSeriesRef) (overlapped bool) {\n505: \tif mSeries.ref != walSeriesRef {\n506: \t\t// Checking if the new m-mapped chunks overlap with the already existing ones.\n507: \t\tif len(mSeries.mmappedChunks) > 0 && len(mmc) > 0 {\n508: \t\t\tif overlapsClosedInterval(\n509: {\n514: \t\t\t\th.logger.Debug(\n515: \t\t\t\t\t\"M-mapped chunks overlap on a duplicate series record\",\n516: \t\t\t\t\t\"series\", mSeries.labels().String(),\n517: \t\t\t\t\t\"oldref\", \t}\n528: \n529: \th.metrics.chunksCreated.Add(float64(len(mmc) + len(oooMmc)))\n530: \th.metrics.chunksRemoved.Add(float64(len(mSeries.mmappedChunks)))\n531: \th.metrics.chunks.Add(float64(len(mmc) + len(oooMmc) - len(mSeries.mmappedChunks)))\n532: \n533: \tif mSeries.ooo != nil {\n534: \t\th.metrics.chunksRemoved.Add(float64(len(mSeries.ooo.oooMmappedChunks)))\n535: \t\th.metrics.chunks.Sub(float64(len(mSeries.ooo.oooMmappedChunks)))\n536: \t}\n537: \n538: \tmSeries.mmappedChunks = mmc\n539: \tif len(oooMmc) == 0 {\n540: \t\tmSeries.ooo = nil\n541: \t} else {\n542: \t\tif mSeries.ooo == nil {\n543: \t\t\tmSeries.ooo = &memSeriesOOOFields{}\n544: \t\t}\n545: \t\t*mSeries.ooo = memSeriesOOOFields{oooMmappedChunks: oooMmc}\n546: \t}\n547: \t// Cache the last mmapped chunk time, so we can skip calling append() for samples it will reject.\n548: \tif len(mmc) == 0 {\n549: \t\tmSeries.mmMaxTime = math.MinInt64\n550: \t} else {\n551: \t\tmSeries.mmMaxTime already be compacted. \tinput            chan walSubsetProcessorInputItem\n577: \toutput           chan []record.RefSample\n578: \thistogramsOutput chan []histogramRecord\n579: }\n580: \n581: type walSubsetProcessorInputItem struct {\n582: \tsamples           []record.RefSample\n583: \thistogramSamples  []histogramRecord\n584: \texistingSeries    *memSeries\n585: \twalSeriesRef const chunkSnapshotPrefix = \"chunk_snapshot.\"\n1295: \n1296: // ChunkSnapshot creates a snapshot of all the series and tombstones in the head.\n1297: // It deletes the old chunk snapshots if the chunk snapshot creation is successful.\n1298: //\n1299: // The chunk snapshot is stored in a directory named chunk_snapshot.N.M and is written\n1300: // using the WAL package. N is the last WAL segment present during snapshotting and\n1301: // M is the offset in segment N upto which data was written.\n1302: //\n1303: // The snapshot first contains all series (each in individual records and not sorted), followed by\n1304: // tombstones (a single record), and finally exemplars (>= 1 record). Exemplars are in the order they\n1305: // were written to the circular buffer.\n1306: func (h *Head) ChunkSnapshot() (*ChunkSnapshotStats, error) {\n1307: \tif h.wal == nil {\n1308: \t\t// If we are not storing any WAL, does not make sense to take a snapshot too.\n1309: \t\th.logger.Warn(\"skipping chunk snapshotting as WAL is disabled\")\n1310: \t\treturn &ChunkSnapshotStats{}, nil\n1311: \t}\n1312: \th.chunkSnapshotMtx.Lock()\n1313: \tdefer h.chunkSnapshotMtx.Unlock()\n1314: \n1315: \tstats := &ChunkSnapshotStats{}\n1316: \n1317: \twlast, woffset, err := h.wal.LastSegmentAndOffset()\n1318: \tif err != nil && !errors.Is(err, record.ErrNotFound) {\n1319: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"get last wal segment and offset: %w\", err)\n1320: \t}\n1321: \n1322: \t_, cslast, csoffset, err := LastChunkSnapshot(h.opts.ChunkDirRoot)\n1323: \tif err != nil && !errors.Is(err, record.ErrNotFound) {\n1324: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"find last chunk snapshot: %w\", err)\n1325: \t}\n1326: \n1327: \tif wlast == cslast && woffset == csoffset {\n1328: \t\t// Nothing has been written to the WAL/Head since the last snapshot.\n1329: \t\treturn stats, nil\n1330: \t}\n1331: \n1332: \tsnapshotName := chunkSnapshotDir(wlast, woffset)\n1333: \n1334: \tcpdir := filepath.Join(h.opts.ChunkDirRoot, snapshotName)\n1335: \tcpdirtmp := cpdir + \".tmp\"\n1336: \tstats.Dir = cpdir\n1337: \n1338: \tif err := os.MkdirAll(cpdirtmp, 0o777); err != nil {\n1339: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"create chunk snapshot dir: %w\", err)\n1340: \t}\n1341: \tcp, err := wlog.New(nil, nil, cpdirtmp, h.wal.CompressionType())\n1342: \tif err != nil {\n1343: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"open chunk snapshot: %w\", err)\n1344: \t}\n1345: \n1346: \t// Ensures that an early return caused by an error doesn't leave any tmp files.\n1347: \tdefer func() {\n1348: \t\tcp.Close()\n1349: \t\tos.RemoveAll(cpdirtmp)\n1350: \t}()\n1351: \n1352: \tvar (\n1353: \t\tbuf  []byte\n1354: \t\trecs [][]byte\n1355: \t)\n1356: \t// Add all series to the snapshot.\n1357: \tstripeSize := h.series.size\n1358: \tfor i := range stripeSize {\n1359: \t\th.series.locks[i].RLock()\n1360: \n1361: \t\tfor _, s := range h.series.series[i] {\n1362: \t\t\tstart := len(buf)\n1363: \t\t\tbuf = s.encodeToSnapshotRecord(buf)\n1364: \t\t\tif len(buf[start:]) == 0 {\n1365: \t\t\t\tcontinue // All contents discarded.\n1366: \t\t\t}\n1367: \t\t\trecs = append(recs, buf[start:])\n1368: \t\t\t// Flush records in 10 MB increments.\n1369: \t\t\tif len(buf) > 10*1024*1024 {\n1370: \t\t\t\tif err := cp.Log(recs...); err != nil {\n1371: \t\t\t\t\th.series.locks[i].RUnlock()\n1372: \t\t\t\t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"flush records: %w\", err)\n1373: \t\t\t\t}\n1374: \t\t\t\tbuf, recs = buf[:0], recs[:0]\n1375: \t\t\t}\n1376: \t\t}\n1377: \t\tstats.TotalSeries += len(h.series.series[i])\n1378: \n1379: \t\th.series.locks[i].RUnlock()\n1380: \t}\n1381: \n1382: \t// Add tombstones to the snapshot.\n1383: \ttombstonesReader, err := h.Tombstones()\n1384: \tif err != nil {\n1385: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"get tombstones: %w\", err)\n1386: \t}\n1387: \trec, err := encodeTombstonesToSnapshotRecord(tombstonesReader)\n1388: \tif err != nil {\n1389: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"encode tombstones: %w\", err)\n1390: \t}\n1391: \trecs = append(recs, rec)\n1392: \t// Flush remaining series records and tombstones.\n1393: \tif err := cp.Log(recs...); err != nil {\n1394: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"flush records: %w\", err)\n1395: \t}\n1396: \tbuf = buf[:0]\n1397: \n1398: \t// Add exemplars in the snapshot.\n1399: \t// We log in batches, with each record having upto 10000 exemplars.\n1400: \t// Assuming 100 bytes (overestimate) per exemplar, that's ~1MB.\n1401: \tmaxExemplarsPerRecord := 10000\n1402: \tbatch := make([]record.RefExemplar, 0, maxExemplarsPerRecord)\n1403: \tenc := record.Encoder{}\n1404: \tflushExemplars := func() error {\n1405: \t\tif len(batch) == 0 {\n1406: \t\t\treturn nil\n1407: \t\t}\n1408: \t\tbuf = buf[:0]\n1409: \t\tencbuf := encoding.Encbuf{B: buf}\n1410: \t\tencbuf.PutByte(chunkSnapshotRecordTypeExemplars)\n1411: \t\tenc.EncodeExemplarsIntoBuffer(batch, &encbuf)\n1412: \t\tif err := cp.Log(encbuf.Get()); err != nil {\n1413: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"log exemplars: %w\", err)\n1414: \t\t}\n1415: \t\tbuf, batch = buf[:0], batch[:0]\n1416: \t\treturn nil\n1417: \t}\n1418: \terr = h.exemplars.IterateExemplars(func(seriesLabels labels.Labels, e exemplar.Exemplar) error {\n1419: \t\tif len(batch) >= maxExemplarsPerRecord {\n1420: \t\t\tif err := flushExemplars(); err != nil {\n1421: \t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"flush exemplars: %w\", err)\n1422: \t\t\t}\n1423: \t\t}\n1424: \n1425: \t\tms := h.series.getByHash(seriesLabels.Hash(), seriesLabels)\n1426: \t\tif ms == nil {\n1427: \t\t\t// It is possible that exemplar refers to some old series. We discard such exemplars.\n1428: \t\t\treturn nil\n1429: \t\t}\n1430: \t\tbatch = append(batch, record.RefExemplar{\n1431: \t\t\tRef:    ms.ref,\n1432: \t\t\tT:      e.Ts,\n1433: \t\t\tV:      e.Value,\n1434: \t\t\tLabels: e.Labels,\n1435: \t\t})\n1436: \t\treturn nil\n1437: \t})\n1438: \tif err != nil {\n1439: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"iterate exemplars: %w\", err)\n1440: \t}\n1441: \n1442: \t// Flush remaining exemplars.\n1443: \tif err := flushExemplars(); err != nil {\n1444: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"flush exemplars at the end: %w\", err)\n1445: \t}\n1446: \n1447: \tif err := cp.Close(); err != nil {\n1448: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"close chunk snapshot: %w\", err)\n1449: \t}\n1450: \tif err := fileutil.Replace(cpdirtmp, cpdir); err != nil {\n1451: \t\treturn chunk snapshots do not cause problems down the line beyond\n1456: \t\t// occupying disk space.\n1457: \t\t// They will just be ignored since a higher chunk snapshot exists.\n1458: \t\th.logger.Error(\"delete old chunk snapshots\", \"err\", err)\n1459: \t}\n1460: \treturn stats, nil\n1461: }\n1462: \n1463: func chunkSnapshotDir(wlast, woffset int) string {\n1464: \treturn fmt.Sprintf(chunkSnapshotPrefix+\"%06d.%010d\", wlast, woffset)\n1465: }\n1466: \n1467: func (h *Head) performChunkSnapshot() error {\n1468: \th.logger.Info(\"creating chunk snapshot\")\n1469: \tstartTime := time.Now()\n1470: \tstats, err := h.ChunkSnapshot()\n1471: \telapsed := time.Since(startTime)\n1472: \tif err != nil {\n1473: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"chunk snapshot: %w\", err)\n1474: \t}\n1475: \th.logger.Info(\"chunk snapshot complete\", \"duration\", elapsed.String(), \"num_series\", stats.TotalSeries, \"dir\", stats.Dir)\n1476: \treturn nil\n1477: }\n1478: \n1479: // ChunkSnapshotStats returns stats about a created chunk snapshot.\n1480: type ChunkSnapshotStats struct {\n1481: \tTotalSeries int\n1482: \tDir         string\n1483: }\n1484: \n1485: // LastChunkSnapshot returns the directory name and index of the most recent chunk snapshot.\n1486: // If dir does not contain any chunk snapshots, ErrNotFound is returned.\n1487: func LastChunkSnapshot(dir string) (string, int, int, error) {\n1488: \tfiles, err := os.ReadDir(dir)\n1489: \tif err != nil {\n1490: \t\treturn \"\", 0, 0, err\n1491: \t}\n1492: \tmaxIdx, maxOffset := -1, \t\t}\n1500: \t\tif !fi.IsDir() {\n1501: \t\t\treturn \"\", 0, 0, fmt.Errorf(\"chunk snapshot %s is not a directory\", fi.Name())\n1502: \t\t}\n1503: \n1504: \t\tsplits := \treturn maxFileName, maxIdx, maxOffset, nil\n1529: }\n1530: \n1531: // DeleteChunkSnapshots deletes all chunk snapshots in a directory below a given index.\n1532: func DeleteChunkSnapshots(dir string, maxIndex, maxOffset int) error {\n1533: \tfiles, err := os.ReadDir(dir)\n1534: \tif err != nil {\n1535: \t\treturn err\n1536: \t}\n1537: \n1538: \tvar errs []error\n1539: \tfor _, fi := range errors.Join(errs...)\n1566: }\n1567: \n1568: // loadChunkSnapshot replays the chunk snapshot and restores the Head state from it. management, record encoding/decoding, corruption repair, and checkpoint creation.\\n\\n## Core WAL Segment Management (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)\\nThe primary WAL implementation in `tsdb/wlog/wlog.go` provides the `WL` struct that manages the write-ahead log lifecycle. Key functions include:\\n- `CreateSegment()` and `OpenWriteSegment()` for segment creation and opening\\n- `NextSegment()` and `NextSegmentSync()` for segment rotation when the current segment reaches size limits (default 128MB)\\n- `Log()` for writing records to the WAL with automatic page flushing (32KB pages) and segment rotation\\n- `Truncate()` for removing old segments after checkpointing\\n- `Segments()` for querying available segment ranges\\nThe WL manages page-based buffering to batch disk writes and ensures records never cross segment boundaries.\\n\\n## Record Encoding/Decoding (tsdb/record/record.go)\\nThe `tsdb/record/record.go` package implements the record encoding format with two main components:\\n- `Encoder` struct that serializes various record types: Series (RefSeries with labels), Samples (RefSample with timestamp/value), Tombstones (deletion markers), Exemplars (RefExemplar), Metadata (RefMetadata with unit/help), and Histogram samples (RefHistogramSample and RefFloatHistogramSample) with custom buckets support\\n- `Decoder` struct that deserializes these record types, handling label encoding/decoding, delta compression for timestamps and series references, and histogram schema validation\\nThe encoding supports compression (Snappy/Zstd) to reduce WAL file size.\\n\\n## WAL Reader Implementations\\nTwo reader implementations handle WAL consumption:\\n- `tsdb/wlog/reader.go` provides the `Reader` struct for reading completed WAL segments with CRC32 checksum validation and record type validation (detecting torn records)\\n- `tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go` provides the `LiveReader` struct for reading WAL segments that are still being written, enabling concurrent WAL processing\\n\\n## Checkpoint Creation (tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go)\\nThe checkpoint system creates compacted snapshots of WAL segments to enable WAL truncation:\\n- `Checkpoint()` function processes WAL segments [from, to], reads records through Decoder, filters old data (based on mint timestamp and keep function), and writes compacted records through Encoder\\n- `LastCheckpoint()` finds the most recent checkpoint directory\\n- `DeleteCheckpoints()` removes old checkpoint directories after WAL truncation\\n- `DeleteTempCheckpoints()` cleans up failed checkpoint attempts\\nCheckpoints are stored in `checkpoint.XXXXXXXX` directories using the same segmented WAL format, enabling easy concatenation with remaining WAL segments.\\n\\n## WAL Corruption Repair (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)\\nThe `Repair()` function handles corruption detection and recovery:\\n- Accepts `CorruptionErr` with segment index and offset information\\n- Deletes all segments after the corrupted segment\\n- Rewrites the corrupted segment by reading valid records up to the corruption point\\n- Creates a new segment for continued writing\\nThis strategy preserves as much data as possible while ensuring consistency.\\n\\n## WAL Watching (tsdb/wlog/watcher.go)\\nThe `Watcher` struct monitors the WAL for changes in real-time:\\n- Implements periodic WAL segment checking and processing\\n- Calls `WriteTo` interface methods to dispatch Series, Samples, Exemplars, Histograms, and Metadata records\\n- Tracks segment indices for series garbage collection\\n- Supports metadata and histogram sample handling\\n\\n## Integration Points\\nThe WAL is integrated with the TSDB head block (tsdb/head_wal.go) which:\\n- Replays WAL records on startup to restore in-memory data\\n- Logs series, samples, and metadata changes during normal operation\\n- Triggers checkpointing based on WAL segment count\\n- Calls `Repair()` on detected corruption errors\\n\\nAll WAL operations are designed to be crash-safe using page-based writes, CRC checksums, and segment atomicity.\"\n}\n",

directories using the same segmented WAL format, enabling easy concatenation with remaining WAL segments.\\n\\n## WAL Corruption Repair (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)\\nThe `Repair()` function handles corruption detection and recovery:\\n- Accepts `CorruptionErr` with segment index and offset information\\n- Deletes all segments after the corrupted segment\\n- Rewrites the corrupted segment by reading valid records up to the corruption point\\n- Creates a new segment for continued writing\\nThis strategy preserves as much data as possible while ensuring consistency.\\n\\n## WAL Watching (tsdb/wlog/watcher.go)\\nThe `Watcher` struct monitors the WAL for changes in real-time:\\n- Implements periodic WAL segment checking and processing\\n- Calls `WriteTo` interface methods to dispatch Series, Samples, Exemplars, Histograms, and Metadata records\\n- Tracks segment indices for series garbage collection\\n- Supports metadata and histogram sample handling\\n\\n## Integration Points\\nThe WAL is integrated with the TSDB head block (tsdb/head_wal.go) which:\\n- Replays WAL records on startup to restore in-memory data\\n- Logs series, samples, and metadata changes during normal operation\\n- Triggers checkpointing based on WAL segment count\\n- Calls `Repair()` on detected corruption errors\\n\\nAll WAL operations are designed to be crash-safe using page-based writes, CRC checksums, and segment atomicity.\"\n}\n",
